Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they used to call this "cure contused", and you should do it for the sick person who has this disease, cut the hairs on their forehead, then make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as deep as two fingers right in the middle of the forehead going down, and the other two at the sides above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries which are at the sides above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the jaw, and let each wound be as deep as three fingers across, joined together; and have a piece of sponge and a lot of bandages ready to wipe up the blood, then insert the spatulum sharply on both sides where the hairline is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision at the temple to the second incision; and scorch all of the skin between the .ii. incisions to the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second incision, then remove this plaster.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument called "culter", which is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other, and it is shaped thus:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the knife's edge towards the chest cavity at the heart, and the flat side towards the bone, and push it in until it reaches the median incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens at the heart, and then make another cut in the median incision to the other defier; and then draw out blood equally, and express the area for the blood taken; then put a tent made of old cotton into each incision, and place dampened cloths in wine and oil and garlic on top, and guard against hot abscesses coming there; and after three days, loosen the ligature, and administer a large amount of cool water, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a constant and habitual catarrh, and you see that the eyes are pale and sunken, and the vision is weakened, and there is pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then you may know from these signs that those matters and this catarrh do not come from one vein only, but from many veins, and that it comes from the brain, and its cure lies therein.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a large slit in the middle of the forehead, and another from the broad nose.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin the incision from the left temple to the right, and cut down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerve that moves the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then pull back between the two lips of the slit, and insert old cotton, and tent with linen; then bind moistened cloths in wine and oil on top, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is healed, you must rub the bone until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with astringent substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice out of it; and administer it to these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear stoppers
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or animals, or stones, or similar objects such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, whether stone or other matter that does not adhere to the ear, nor grow in the ear, then put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, drop some violet oil or oil of wormwood onto it, then administer an enema. Let the patient sneeze from the congestion, and plug their nostrils when they sneeze, and place pieces of cloth or wool around their ears; let the ears be on top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	It often comes out through this treatment; and if it doesn't come out, then administer an enema with thin forceps, of which there is a description later.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it pops out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, then perform an extraction using a small, thin needle of soft metal; and if it does not pop out in this way, make a brass hook and insert its tip firmly into the ear canal, and plug the area around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull outward firmly, for often it will come out in this way as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take some glue and attach a bird to it, and place some instrument designed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull outward.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all these things that we have said, then be quick to split the ear so that an abscess forms there, and a spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first make the patient fast for three days, and draw blood according to his condition, then have him sit between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small slit in the root of the ear at the fat where it depends; and the slit should be shaped like a moon, so that you reach the stone, then extract it according to your ability, and suck it strongly with your mouth; and treat it until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is in and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatule, held subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision on that spot.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grains are moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then pull it out with thin forceps and with a suction cup, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute conditions when fluid drains into the ear, the patient should first sneeze from congestion, and open the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that very ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many small stones according to the length of your index finger, thin and light, and heat them in fire; and put one of these stones into the ear, and let it fall on its side from another part, and pierce with another stone upon the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and so it will come out entirely. If you see that, then take a straw and push one end into the ear and the other end with fire until the longer straw burns; then do likewise with other straws until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is a small body like a flea or similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is a large body that one can feel, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section and tract on distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must examine the ear in the sun; if any worms appear, then pull them out with fine tweezers, and if none appear, then take the quill of a goose feather and pierce the eardrum.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	It is tight below and loose above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the narrowest end of the instrument into the ear according to the amount of suffering from the ailment, then suck strongly on the tube; do this frequently until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if it does not come out, then plug the ear with cotton as I have said about the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the treatment of worms, and you will find them in the section on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a small hole underneath and holes above for distilling; and to press the distillate into the instrument with a well-made brass instrument for this purpose, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around the blade; then pour your oil or juice and any remedies you wish into the quill, and the quill is in the ear; then place the razor over the cotton and press your hand gently so that the remedy is distilled onto the eardrum; and the patient feels it inside, and the distillation is a little warm from the fire so that it is not too cold when it enters the ear; and guard against it being too hot, for the remedy would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear stoppers
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to men due to a wound or a growth within the ear, and sometimes this stopper occurs deep within the ear, so it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is only a slight displacement of the opening, which can be easily seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it occurs deep within the ear and cannot be seen, it is a difficult condition in many ways, and in such cases, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane visible, then observe how the stopper forms.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed at the front and back, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the membrane is due to a growth or the body of the ear, then grip it with тонé pins, and gently peel it away until all the growth is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the growth is deep in the ear, take a narrow, thin razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the oppression from which those who are affected greatly suffer when they hear it, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a plug in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed; then take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder over powdered vitriol; and if you see any swelling in the ear, you should draw out the tent and replace it with another tent moistened with cerate made from olive oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and apply it to the ear; and use other treatments that stop the bleeding from the distilling veins.
de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This poultice comes from plants when they are moist and dry; you should spread it with tweezers and tongs, and the root of a spathe; then put powdered vitriol on top.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if there is no scurf, cauterize it with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision heals; and many times they return, until nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times they come in paper form, things that look like hailstones in shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "hail," and it is a gathering of thick moisture on top and bottom; the treatment is such: take care if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and that is an easy thing to know; then make it wide, then peel each part gently, then grab it with tweezers and pluck it out.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot pluck it without piercing the paper a little, then do not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, then stitch it up, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, then do not use force, for ointments will heal it quickly and close it up.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and grasp the hailstone with tweezers and squeeze from both sides; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is crushed, wash the eye with salted water, and clean the area of any pus until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat around the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinch is a fat that is ensnared in the webs of paper above, and this happens most to children with no one else, and it is very painful for them, and they get the catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces, and sleep on top of it, and their papers are underneath their eyelids moistened by the inflammation and appearance covered by the exinch that opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinch between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the treatment is that the patient places his head on your lap; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, and then place it over the eye; and press with your fingers from both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moist area with a spatulum, making the incision no larger than the wound made for vein opening; and in various cases, the exinach comes out through the incision, depending on its shape like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	So take a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and move your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to touch the fissure, or you will reach all the way to the eye and blister it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrescence opens at the beginning of the fissure, gently widen the fissure slightly so that it appears; then pull as we have said, and moisten clothes in vinegar and water, and place them on the area, and apply bandages tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind seal and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hot abscess in that place, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.And if there is a hot abscess in that place, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hair of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers, uneven and different from their natural state, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases, such as tears, softening of the papers, and white film, leading to destruction of the eyes; there are four ways to treat this: through cauterization with fire, or with a medicine applied directly to the eye, or through incision and stitching, or with canes, depending on what I will describe.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's eye in your dominant hand, then turn the eyelid to the left; if it returns to its original position, that is good; otherwise, insert a needle and thread through the eyelid, close to the edge of the discolored area where the uneven hairs are growing, and run the thread over the entire eyelid. Then, with a scalpel, make an incision under the eyelid, along the uneven hairs, from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small piece of cotton and cloth under the eyelid. Mark a figure eight on the eyelid, like the shape of a myrrh roll, but the shape should correspond to the amount you see the eyelid raising or distorting.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if to someone who needs it, cut a great quantity of the paper according to how soft the paper is; then, mark all over the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large nostril until small; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a hair root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the heart, then cut it all off; then sew together the two lips with a single thread of fine wool using a needle, and draw out the blood, and dry up the excess threads on both nostrils using anything sticky, if you see fit to do so; and if not, pay no attention, then leave the sewing and the threads for three or four days; then heal the wound without sewing with dry and constricting things, because the paper lifts up at the sudden healing of the wound and its unification, but the sewing is painful (as the ancients said), and this work is done without fear; and there is another way: it is to mark the paper in a shape that is also like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three branches according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out those on top with small scissors evenly according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the object is not aligned, then take a needle and thread it through the center of the wound; and thread another piece of thread through the large hole of the ear, and the second thread through the small one, and tie the threads together between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin you have marked, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing, and treat it until it heals; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hair of the paper is converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of warts is as follows: you must first turn the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, then make two warts using art, and two thin lines as long and wide as the spatumile; then tie two knots at both ends where you hold the threads; then bring one knot close to the other gently above the paper on the eye, and pull the two warts from their roots; leave them like that for a few days, and the skin that was pulled will die and harden and fall off as it shrinks.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow to heal, and the wound has strength, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn and the paper is lifted, and the hairs no longer hurt; and this is the form of the two chains that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the tools are such that you thread a thin needle with a fine silk thread, then tie the ends together gently and make the length of the threads about a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the spatumile, and tie the end of this thread as well; then put the patient's head in your lap, and let them face the sun so that their skin is exposed, for it is a delicate treatment; then thread the needle all the way into the root of the hair close to the skin until you draw it out through the paper with the natural hair; then pull the hair all the way up to the spatumile, and insert the hair into the spatumile along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will treat the hunt underneath to the very end that you have ordered, until the hunt comes out of the hole above and you see it through the vision of the eye; then you will treat the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany it with a long hair from the horses' mane, and let it grow with that which you leave, until it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eyelash
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "alacrity" or warts comes in the eye, it happens in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a cut, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment for it is that you split the sore, and loosen the edges of it, and put in tenters of linen, and let it heal; and you must not use in its cure anything that would dry it out and constrict it.Et si li tentier ne se pot acostumer a la soudure, ou s’ele ne voudra estre fendee, si covient que tu le traites de l’altra maniere, et qu’il soit tenus en la cure de li, si com te dit en li章es ci-dessus.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And if the tent cannot be accommodated to the sore, or it will not open up, then you must treat it in the other way, and care for it as described above in the chapters. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; rosewater, or water made from dill, and linseed cooked, and ointment of dried olives melted in some oil, and wrap a tent around it, and care for it thus.Et si li maladie vient de la seconde maniere, si covient que tu traites li membre en la cure de li come si il estoit natureil; et s’ele viengne d’une contumace et d’un mal engin, si convint que les tentes soient en l’huile de lin, et l’arose d’aigue, ou en altée.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is to ensure that it does not fuse according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have spoken of are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is below, is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; the way to treat them is to take a needle with a double thread, pierce the skin on one side so that the thread goes through both ears of the jaw, then the meat above the needle, and the cup to the large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that's good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper over, and make two cuts along the edges inside the paper; and the ears of the two cuts should be the two angles of the incision you have peeled, and make angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of the letter "I" in Greek; then remove the meat, according to the quantity that its sides are cut under, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with soft medicines and poultices until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a split or a stitch or cautery, then one must make a clean split underneath the hairs of the paper, and according to what is stated above; then unravel between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares remedies with all his might, so that the figure returns to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness happens to human beings in such a way that the paper above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then one must therefore push the tip of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and hold it with tweezers, so as to grasp what is cut in the subtle spatula, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient does not feel that the spatula is too sharp or cutting into the eye; and make your incision, by which you peel away this membrane, very lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and when all of this membrane has been removed, there may sometimes be a sore in the eye, and it should be washed with warm water and then with cool water, and then a tent of linen should be placed between the paper and the eye, and lamb's wool dampened in egg white should be laid over the eye; and after the third day, one should use collyrium and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that there are two types of ulcer: one is nervous and resembles a hard ulcer, and the other is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture; when touched with iron and pinched, it feels like paneling to the fingernails, but no one can feel it. Both types begin at the outer corner of the eye, growing little by little until they cover the entire eye, obscure its light, and impair its movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is to have the patient place his head against your hand, then work the eyelids; and hold the paper in your hand, then pinch the edge of the ulcer with tiny pincers and stretch it upward; next take a needle and thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox's hair through it, and double over the point of the needle slightly before inserting it into the ulcer, and tie the ulcer with a thread and stretch it upward, then scrape along the edge of the ulcer from its base toward the eyebrow until you reach the tear gland, using tiny movements and leaving the natural flesh of the tear gland untouched, so that the incision does not affect the flow of tears; sometimes only the edge of the ulcer needs to be tied, as we have said, with thread, then scrape along the spatumile:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatumile does not touch the fleshy membrane and rupture it, and that the tear gland is not pierced; after the incision, drop a little powdered chalk into the eye, and make a collar out of litarge, leaving it in place until the next day; then treat the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push in the needle, and the hook cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured by medicines; and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the malady, and take the spatule lightly poked according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail gently, and if you see that it is not lessened and the reason is pressing, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litarge and red copper ore, ground together, and stop the eye until the next day; then start the other work according to this same method, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then start the work again as before, until it is healed.Si li ungle est ost, adonques tu le remets, et si li est alongie, adonques tu le rompts; car il ne poait demorer a son leu.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the arm hurts the eye greatly through great harm, then suspend it at the elbow, and cut off a part and not all, so that the body of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men, a red lump sometimes appears on the tip of the penis, covering it and pressing against the foreskin, resembling a rosebud; the treatment is to place the patient's head over yours, then work on the lump, and press all the lump towards the nail bed with firm pressure; then cut into the first lump and continue cutting all the way to the root, being careful not to hurt the eye during the procedure; and let the incision be as deep as a spider web, as described in the section on nail incisions, and use gentle force to remove it, as demonstrated in this chapter; once the incision is complete and all the lump removed, apply oil of sea-brook or similar corrosive medicine, and place cotton soaked in egg white over the eye to secure it; if nothing remains, and the cold pain persists, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until the eye is healed, and do the same for any other lumps that appear in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless you should ease the treatment of every weak part of the natural way; and in accidental work with iron, do not put your hand into any of those works until you see that this member can bear such work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Thus are red veins which are covered on the eye, and tolerates one's vision and weakens the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary, first, that you examine the eye, because in this way it is, it is swollen and there is no other disease except the redness; then he should be treated in this way: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then gently squeeze those veins all around according to his skill, and let the fingers be twice as subtle according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two compresses be in degrees in .i. body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you can squeeze these veins gently, and let the blood flow out an hour after another, until you see the veins recede from the eye; and be careful not to cut the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not slip outside these veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye green and red color to corrupt what is left of the scabies.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to squeeze all of this in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye of soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for a few days until the pain is relieved and there is a hot abscess, then begin again according to what is written above until he is healed; and this is the way of doing it:
de la fistule de l’oil	of eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Examine the fistula, which is called "arissati" in Latin: when you cure it with cautery and medicine that burns according to what I have written before, and it is not healed, then there is a wound in it where you should cut into the abscess, the place where it should be, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, you will see the decay and blackness; there is the instrument of which this is the form; it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron into a flat head, and punctured like a file as it is in its current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the location of the decayed bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little so that you know the decay has been removed; do this several times, then restore the site with astringent medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if it is glued and the skin grows on it, and the body of the bow is glued and remains so for 40 days, and does not renew itself and is not abscessed, and nothing bad happens to it, you will know that he is healed; if not, there is no other way than to bring the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form: then uncover the bone again by fire, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take up the iron forest according to this form, and let the head of the iron be three-pointed, and the rod be thinned until the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then he puts it on the bone of the arm, and moves his hand away from the eye a little, then returns to press down with all his might until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it through the wind that enters if he holds his hand over his nose; then dry up the wound with medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh heals and hardens, examine the matter in the nose; this is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully and there is no disturbance to the eye or diminution, then you must ligate the patient; then cleanse the eye, then place leeches or a cupping glass without piercing to draw out any fluid; then apply an ointment made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla over the eye, and then compress it with bandages and cloth. The manner of the bandages is that you take soft cloth, double each one over four times, and then place one over another according to the quantity that the eye requires; then compress it firmly from above with a hard bandage, and repeat the leeches to draw without piercing; then remove the leeches and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the ligature becomes soft, you must compress it tightly; then remove the ligature after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then repeat the ointment and the bandages and the ligature and the leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from a torn woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in woven fabric, then it opens and appears like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you pierce an needle in the root of the part below up to the part above; and then pierce another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the armhole; and tie the fabric around the eye, and compress it well, then remove the needle and place a soft egg-soaked cloth over the eye; and leave it until the threads tear with the fabric, then cleanse the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is constrained by the fabric in a circle of cloth all around, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great indication, then pierce them with a sharp spatulate instrument which enters through the eye socket, and scrape away the white moisture and bring the eyes down, and enter inside immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called «alcunnati» is nothing but a membrane gathered in the eye, resembling a descending pus, but it is not pus; and the manner of its appearance in the treatment is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take his head in your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the membrane coming above your eyes; then it should be pinched, and the light should go down, and the patient should see things as he used to; and if it does not go under, know that it is pus, and if the descending membrane is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatulum and gently probe the conjunctiva with it, and with the cornea and the crown, until the membrane is released; and when it is released, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the diseases in the division, and what should be done to pierce them; now act according to the state of health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands away from sunlight, and press his healthy eye tightly shut; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right; then take in your right hand, if it is the left eye, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if it is the right eye; then insert the tip of the instrument along the edge of the cornea by the thickness of a hair into the white part of the eye near the edge of the lower eyelid, and gently press the instrument until it penetrates the white part of the eye, and you will feel that «almagda» reaches the empty space; and the depth of «almagda’s» path should be equal to the thickness of the space between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the cornea, and then insert the instrument up to the level where the water is, then express it under one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain descends now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the pain ascends the second way, push the instrument gently while turning your hand a little, and when it is lodged and does not move, then extract it gently in a twisting motion; then put in a little sea-gem and remove the eye from it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then, push the eye out with force, using a wet sponge or lamb's wool in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and bind it with clean cloth.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on a mixture of comfrey with an abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almgada cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you must use the instrument called 'albarit', which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so, pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the slit fine, then insert the instrument gently as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare for the patient a dark room in which he sleeps on his back in a dim place; and let him be free of all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head to the right or left, and let him be bound according to his condition for three days; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten it so that the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	if such an abscess comes, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and receive from him who soothes an abscess; and when it is soothed, then loosen the view and put on his face the small gold edge to cover some sore, and let him be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go out of the house little by little, and return to your own case; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iran, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, and suck out the water, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagest, because those who do not know them will see them; and they are properly made of bronze.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads be of the same subtle metal, and the rear in 3 angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or born dogs with diverse deformities, from which some seem like scorpions with many feet; and so there are some with a deformation of a dark color, and some with a light-colored sore.Et il y en a qui sont com sanz teinture, et si i a qui est char ou piez ou au vis ou a la main, ou a autre part de son corp, si doit li chevalliers covrir sa paie et l’huem, et aler a l’ecole et demourer en telle maison.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case, for the wagon which is flat and not curved, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, pour vinegar on the wagon, and pull it out; then grab what you can hold with a thin spatula from one side, until you know that the wagon has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains which one cannot cover, then open it at its thinnest and lightest part, so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess forms, then lancing as appropriate; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the evil is removed, then apply ice or cold water and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostrils open and moisture reaches the palate, you will know he is cured; and if moisture does not pass through as it should, you will know there is a foreign body in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach: therefore, you must insert a fairly thick thread of linen, knotted at one end, leaving some space between each knot, about the thickness of a finger or less; then make the patient hold the end of the thread in his nostril with as much force as he can, and pull it gently through until it comes out through the mouth; many children do this at school, and it is an easy matter for anyone who wishes to do so. Then hold one end of the thread which is coming out of the nostril in one hand, and the other end which is coming out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull them gently apart while holding them close to your nose.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the nails have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the nail, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointments corrode all that is left of the flesh; and then put a plug of linen in the nose for several days until it heals, and if he needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, through which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and it must also be straight; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be filled for cleansing the nose; and there should be a handle on the instrument to hold it while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the nose and grows and becomes large, to such an extent that it is visible to the eye; therefore one should cut it at the beginning and remove the whole pustule, then place on the fire cautery or burning medicine; but if one delays cutting it until it has become large, take care whether it is hard, discolored in color, and of poor sensation: then do not touch it with iron, for it is an encrusted abscess; because when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due to pressure rather than discoloration, and you see that one can cover it all, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been cut and sewn up
