Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuance comes in one of these soft cartilage-like things, it benefits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, examine whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; then bring together the two lips with a stitch, then heal it until it is cured; and if the lips are peeled on both sides, then you should scrape away all parts of their skin until they heal, then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and tie them, and apply powder upon powder of dragon's blood and incense ground; and place over the powders a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster, and leave it so that it may heal by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is cured.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the abdomen; or with thread, as I have already informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hollows of the lips there are hard abscesses, similar to grains of wheat, small and large; therefore you must split the lips, and cut into each pustule with pincers, and scrape away the pus from every part; then apply powdered vitriol to the incision, until the blood is dried up; then use raw garlic, and clean the area of any dried matter until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a tooth grows on the gums, which the elders call «albulus»; one should hold it with tweezers and cut at its root, and let the blood or puss flow; then place powdered vitriol or other binding and dessicating powders over the site; and if that tooth comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, then cut it again and cauterize it: if it does not come back after cauterization, then it will not return. These are the forms of treatment for teeth.
des sordens	of the eyes
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, and there are ugly and rough growths; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, as far as the corruption extends to the gum, and the teeth stink; so one should have the patient hold his head steady with his jaw in your lap, and you should pick at the teeth or growths that are visible, until nothing remains; and thus you should do with the blackness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are all cleaned out; and if it is removed on the first attempt, that is good; if not, then one must repeat the procedure again the next day or the third, until everything is cleaned out; and know that teeth require diverse forms of tools for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, so that the pick used to clean between the teeth has different forms from those used to clean the teeth themselves; and these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure a tooth of its pain, you should hurry to pull it out as far as you can, because one must not delay in doing so; for there is no excuse for not pulling it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is compelled to withdraw, you must be certain about the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient and believes it to be in a sound tooth, and so he has the healthy tooth pulled out; and yet the pain is not alleviated through this as long as the decayed tooth remains, for we have already tried this with those healers; and when you are quite certain about the toothache, then you must scrape around the tooth all the way to the gum; then move it with your fingers or with subtle tweezers bit by bit, until it is well loosened, then grip it firmly with the tweezers; and let the patient's head be in your lap, and hold it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, pull out the tooth firmly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of those instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you must fill the hole with pieces of cloth, and gently pinch it with tweezers so that it does not break while being pulled; and one must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it and leave a part behind, which will cause greater pain due to the root's toxicity.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be wary of acting like ignorant healers who, in their haste and arrogance, sometimes break the tooth, not heeding what we have advised; they sometimes cause great illness through the toxicity of the roots left behind or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. Once the tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine or garlic and salt; if bleeding occurs, which is common, apply ground vitriol; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of forceps, which are silent in the teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so they do not double when you pull the tooth. And these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made of iron, and they should be toothed to hold the roots.
de la racine des dens	of the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the roots remain in the tissue, then you must put moist cotton on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is soft, then insert the forceps called "algefri", which make the shoulder look like a sick bird's beak. They should be made like a file, and that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is made of ivory, thus its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, whose forms come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should also use this instrument with .ij. tweezers, of which the form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are before in the reason of teeth, and with this instrument that resembles a large pair of tweezers, of which the form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that there are many instruments of teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise subtle master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are some diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it does not break from the carriage or other bones, or it protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, that I have told you about, and helps with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but he can hold and remove it; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines, and if there is protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then he should treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to nature and its shape is ugly, especially in virgins, then you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or polished; then pull it out; and if there is air with the tooth, take this instrument of which here is the form, and it is like a small beak, and let it be of iron sharpened at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And pull it gently day by day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a type of file like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the lime that needles are made from; and with the lime, lightly prick the tooth little by little, so that it does not move until it chips; then smooth it at the end with a file completely, and if the tooth is too sharp and bites into the tongue, then file down the sharpness so that it neither bites nor corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loose from either pushing or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what he eats without defecating, and you have tried restricting medicines, but it does not work; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never moves. The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. And if you see the teeth leaning towards each other, take the wire and wrap it double between two healthy teeth, then put the shoulder between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again up to where you started, and pull your hand gently and with force, so that it does not move. Your aim should be at the root of the tooth, so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the teeth with tweezers, and bring them together, and fit them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not bite the tongue; and then leave it thus tightly as long as it can stay, and if it becomes loose, or the wire breaks, then tighten it with another wire; let it remain and serve in this way for its entire lifetime, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two defective ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth chips, if it is put back in its place, freshly and as we have said; and only a wise and experienced person should attempt this, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth out of cow's bone, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and restrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes under the tongue, either by nature from birth, or by accident from a wound; and the treatment is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and has his head in your healthy mouth, and holds his tongue; then grasp the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its housing, and if there is hardening or swelling, and this is from a sudden wound, then it pierces with the hook and grasps the ligament widely; and be careful that the slit is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, then raise the place with rosewater and garlic, or with cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen; and tie the patient's head every night so that the lips do not adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood oozes out, then apply ground glass to the site; and if the wound bleeds, then cauterize it with a lenteginous cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it further until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it discolored to a dusky or black color, and the patient does not feel any pain, do not touch it because it is a ulcer. If it is declining towards a phlegmon and there is moisture, insert the claw and open it with a spatulum, releasing it from both sides. If bleeding occurs due to your action, apply ground vitriol until it stops; then return to your treatment, continuing until you have removed everything. Afterwards, apply aqua rosa and aqua silice, and treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are growths in the throat called 'godath', and they are properly called 'almonds'. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, then be careful: if they are hard abscesses of a small size with a light color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron because of bloodletting; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will burst it, or it will burst by itself; and if it is a white color and the root is thin, have ready an instrument for cauterizing, but first check that the abscess is cool and has calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your shade, and open his mouth and hold the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue underneath all of it, with which is made the form; and it should be of silver or thin bronze just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	While pressing the tongue with this instrument, you will see the abscess. Take a pair of tweezers and grab it, then pull it up into the tonsil and out from the top as hard as you can; pull some of the threads along with it, then cover the instrument with a cloth, which is part of its shape, so that it looks like a fork. The prongs are curved, one facing one way and the other facing the opposite way, and they are very sharp, made from iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, use a pair of tongs with the same shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it has a sharp edge on one side and a flat edge on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and with water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water, or with peels of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them then just as the two tonsils are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, specifically a small abscess; and she had a very closed throat, so much so that the woman could not breathe through the opening that was blocked, nor eat or drink, and would have died if it continued like that for another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so much that it had forced out two holes in the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened therefore, and inserted a hook into one of the nostrils, then drew it out forcefully, and cut away a large portion of the abscess; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the hook into the abscess and scraped away at it, and only a little blood came out; and thus I cleared the passage of the throat of the woman, and she was now able to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut away at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess regrew and filled up the space that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; therefore, I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it remained without growing; and I left these parts, and may God help her after me.
de l’uve	from the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When a tumor descends into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round beneath, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and that which is round and not long, and is blood-red or flesh-colored or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have described, of its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument of which I have spoken before; then insert the probe into the eye, and cut beneath, and scoop it out using one of the two instruments that I have mentioned for the incision of the two almond-shaped areas.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover anything more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it will grieve the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two testicles, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear due to covering, then you should use the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is for acute fever.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then presses his tongue against the instrument we described in the chapter on cautery, and breathes in with hot breath, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and he employs the movement of this instrument, from which comes its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and has a handle on the top where one puts the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and one places the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucous flow from his mouth due to the medicine, so that it does not descend into the throat and cause bleeding; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for the amount of half an hour, until you see it becoming numb and the bites of the medicine calm down; and if you see [this], take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all the way into the eye with the cotton on top, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after 4 or 5 days. And if you need to repeat the cautery of the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cautery, wash around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and use rosewater, and cure it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put garlic in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well-glazed with strong clay, and in the pot there is one instrument with a handle according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one of the lips pressed into the patient's mouth so that the vapour rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is mortified; afterwards, he should do this often, until the eye dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for various things can happen there; nor do this beyond the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside it the yolk of an egg, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg yolk does not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, becomes stuck in the throat; therefore you must try to pull it out as far as you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your strength, so that you can feel the object moving; and if it does not come loose and remains stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or let the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel-wool, or a lettuce root, or a dry crumb of bread; and tie a string to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches the spot, it will lodge there, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have described, take a leaden instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be bent at one end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the upper part lifted up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest you harm it, nor push the bone in; and move the patient's head so that he vomits, in order for the object to come out; then let him swallow the instrument again, or pull it out with the instrument, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is drawn, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the sick person towards the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine tweezers that are fit for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a curved cane, and put it into the throat of the sick person, then put on the curve of the cane hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take some cold water and open your mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with your hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, let it flow out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not flow out as we have said, then suffocate the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for fumigating the throat; do this several times, for it will come out without harm.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to do the fumigation is to put burning charcoal in a pot, and place over it a perforated cover, and put the instrument's head into the hole; then pour in your fumigating agent, and the patient should place the end of their throat inside their mouth, close their mouth so the smoke does not escape, but rather goes into their blood; and the blood will flow out now, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation several times; and let the patient endure thirst, and eat salted and dry things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for them to go to the toilet.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the throat looks like bent tongs so as to be able to enter the throat; it resembles a bird's beak and has roughness from sandpaper so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; see the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many types of abscess appear, according to what memory brings hereafter from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways of which the one is in its appearance itself, and that which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundations, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses which one must not pierce until the bowels are dead according to their fulfillment; and there are some that one must pierce when they are crud, and they do not die according to their fulfillment, as with abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when abscesses come from these joints, and one lets them be as long as they are swollen around the edge, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, by which that is caused to contract in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay to open it until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; but if it is on the bottom, one should open it in such a way that it does not burst outward, and it can become long inside, and then there will be a fistula, and it cannot heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to its maturity, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishment of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the piercing in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears soft; and let the piercing be deep in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and on nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who are bent, according to the affected member.Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the puncture until it is confirmed by completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	Because if you puncture it before that, the venom will flow through the body, and it will be filled with much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for any abscess that is punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must treat small abscesses with small openings; and large abscesses with large openings, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where one should cut the skin, and cover it up; when it has become like a piece of cloth, and is deadened, then one should do as one does with blisters: and there are some that are split into three angles, and some which one covers like a myrtle leaf; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial boil, you should pierce it plainly; and when the boil is large and has formed a great pus pocket, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a portion; then stop up the boil until the next day, then draw out some more; do this several times from great to small, until all the pus is drained; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying child, or a young child, or an elderly decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus may sometimes spurt out with the opening of the boil, and the patient might die from it, and you would not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution; and when you have pierced your boil, wash the wound, and examine if the wound of the boil is small; and if it is a plain incision, apply tenters made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large boil, and there are many openings, then you should insert a tent in each opening so that they press against each other; and if you have cut into the boil a portion of the skin, and lifted it up all around, then you should fill it with dry cotton or rasped linen without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flow occurs due to your work, administer cold water and vinegar, and moisten the cloth, and place it over the flowing area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood flow persists, administer treatment and care, and the powders I mentioned with my own hands in this book; and if it is during winter, and the area on the abscess is very nervous, then you should place wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cool wine and oil, for a third of a day, as we have said; and then open the abscess, wash and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you should know generally about the treatment of abscesses. I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and you have the chapter here.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the head come small abscesses, and they are caused by us being in fabrics, like the goiter on a goose's neck, and there are many variations of them.Et si li chief est hote, et li leus ou li aposteme est hote, si covient que tu mettes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue fraiche, jusc’au tier jor; puis deslie l’aposteme, essue li leus, et cure-le si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and others that are moist like pus; and there are some that are hard and stone-like in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the abdomen is that you must examine all instruments called "endoscopies", from which the form comes later, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will cut it from above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, they scrape without leaving anything the skin that contains the moisture, because it returns again if nothing is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will heal.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then cotton is applied again, as before, on the second and third day, until you are sure that it no longer hurts at night; then the wound is treated with ointment as appropriate until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus, open it according to this method, deeply; and squeeze your fingers, and scrape off all of the scabs, and apply all of your treatment by pulling outward through the cot, where he lies; and if the artery makes a sound contrary to what I have said, then do as I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat an abscess if it is stone-like, and cut and treat it as I have told you.Si li artere clent, si la traie fuer l’aposteme sus la cotte, tant que li sang ne s’en poie; et si le sang est gras, si met sel et vinyer, et remue li cot ains qu’il s’escanse, et distrai li sang; et se li sang ne s’escante pas, si traie li cot ou il gist sus l’aposteme, tant qu’il s’escanse par le siel de li cotte.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the pus-filled, moist abscess is lighter, because there is less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses have no moisture in them, and I found one such abscess in the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be crushed; and if one had broken it, it would have caused a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come in the head, unlike those that occur in children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be at the most dependent location to allow pus to drain; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and some are connected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within the chest, as are the abscess and swelling in the head, as we have said; and there are many similar scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that do not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	For those in which you see a good disposition to touch, and are similar in color to the body, and move from all sides and are not enlarged towards the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and are not deep; you should cut it from above and scrape off each part, and be careful that you do not cut into the nerve or vein, and do not use the spatula or scalpel so that the hand slips, and do not go too far ahead, but only as much as you need.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you grasp the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put into the wound vitriol ground, or any powders that stop blood, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess is eased, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it; then consult your right index finger if any small scrofula remains, then pick and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if he has a large vein in the root of the scrofula, you must not pick that scrofula at its root, but ligature it with a double strong thread, and let it hang without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut around the entire scrofula, then you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, since there is no longer any surplus due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should proceed to cut around the root of it and pull it out, then sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Scrofula that holds surplus material, pierce it where it appears to be dying; and pierce it as previously described, hanging from the wound, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and once the wound is clean, use ointment to encourage the growth of flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of throat surgery, but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with scrofula, the flap of flesh in the throat called the "epiglottis" should be cut away; and this is done to help those with an abscess that is hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.Si li maladie est en la gorge, il covient que tu fendures la gorge et li pormon dou costé, car il ne peut aler si non.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it below three circles or four at a small slit across the two circles, or depending on the size of the slit, not in the cartilage; and those places which are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to the Adam's apple, then split the windpipe until it reaches the larynx; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then close the wound, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe of the larynx which jumps out through the hole that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it up completely without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient judged dead, and the lack of breath evident.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot choke, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and because of this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease was passed, and it passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and to treat it, once it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden take a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the muscles of her neck; and I was called to heal her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that blood had issued from it, and I judged that she had not coughed up any blood or vomited anything other than through her throat, and the blood was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was cured; and the maiden had no scar but that her voice was hoarse, and afterward she returned to her former state; therefore I say that one should have no fear of cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess the color of a grape, and it occurs often in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; the natural type has no cause.The accidental type occurs when something becomes stuck in the throat and the person tries to vomit it out but cannot. Instead, the object is forced into the windpipe and causes an abscess there. The patient suffers great pain and, if not treated quickly, dies. If the object is large, such as a bone, it must be cut up with a knife before it can be extracted from the throat.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidents are according to two ways, one of which is similar to a cyst, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it is not appropriate to operate by making incisions except in the small ones, and test and examine all the entrance: if you find it just as the cyst, and cannot be opened at all, cut it, just as we cut a cyst, and treat it throughout its coat, if there is any; and examine thoroughly, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many types of cysts, of which I will describe all the similarities; and now I must explain all the differences between a cyst and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that childbirth is a fever and heat that lasts until the delivery is complete and the placenta is expelled; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a cyst, there is no heat, fever or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body; it starts like a pimple and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, dry or moist, and their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the pustule, that you examine and inquire into it first with all the instruments called "entromissoires", according to what its form will allow, as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses in the brain is to squeeze in the wettest place that you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core; then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the instrument and take care not to let anything escape.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus runs clear, whatever color it may be, they should proceed as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the instrument no pus comes out, know that it is solid, so they should cut into it in the shape of a cross, seize it with forceps, and gently scrape away the skin on each side, guarding the membrane underneath which they draw it out intact; and if they cannot draw it out intact, then they should cut it away piece by piece until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it stays nothing, it will return to the nose many times; and if something remains, without causing you grief, employ corrosive powders on the wound, constrict the wound, and apply hot poultices for abscesses, and treat with other remedies until healed; and if the nostril is large, cut both lips of the wound, and treat with that which produces pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is bleeding profusely or otherwise behaving contrary to how it should, then hasten and apply ground vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound scabs over; then return to using what was previously effective.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the trocar, which are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of holes that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb"; and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of warts are very varied, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are warts that have two curves in three ways; and there are warts that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are warts that have two curves, and warts with only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these knives have cutting edges, and some only cut from one side, so that the vein or nerve is not cut; and these instruments are used in many ways, so that the patient does not suffer when opening abscesses; and they are in three forms: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are only used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes another small instrument is made, similar to a slice of wood, according to this form, with which blood is stopped.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes it is placed in the place that heals by opening veins and arteries, and sometimes they are bound according to this large form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	At times the breasts of some men swell when they become corrupt, looking like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen. Anyone who wishes to treat them should follow this recipe from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward, scrape off the fat and treat the wound with a caustic poultice, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and heal it until it is cured; and if the breast sags downward and becomes soft due to its size as happens to women, then make two slits on it from above in the shape of similar cuts; so that one side holds the other at the end of one slit and the other slit, so that the larger slit contains the smaller according to this form, from line b to g; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and administer what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment until it is healed. If it is not healed or the incision is not fully done due to the patient's discomfort or blood flow, you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it absorbs the remainder of the fat and the skin, then heal it until it is cured.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels which are in the abscess have been emptied, employ the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofula, they should proceed as we have said in slits for scrofula; and if the wound becomes swollen, they should apply cauterization as we have said previously.Et se li apostemes est desoz le col ou desoz les asseles, si covient que il soit fendu a la radice selonc la ligne m. jusc’a la ligne .g., car en cest lieu il conviens que il soit fenduz selonc la ligne de la nature.
de la routure de l’artere	on the rot of an artery
