Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is open and the skin above it, this often leads to abscesses, and also causes the vein to swell and become abscessed; and one can recognize this when it is due to the artery, as the abscesses are long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, there is a tugging sensation; and when it is due to a vein, there is a hard lump beneath the skin; and it is foolishness to cover these abscesses, especially when they are on the joints and at the angles and in the neck and many other places, and they are large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one should avoid cauterizing with iron, and if it is on the head, one should also avoid cauterizing there; and when it is an abscess due to a swollen artery, one should cut through the skin above it along its length, and then carefully cut away the artery from the surrounding tissue, so that it is exposed; then insert a needle beneath the skin at the center of the abscess, and pierce it all the way through to the other side, and tie off the artery with a double thread in two places, according to how I instructed you for the extraction of the two temporal arteries; then poke the spot between the two threads with an introducer until the pus comes out, and then release the abscess; then apply a poultice of hot bowels, until the thread cuts through the skin; then treat it with suitable ointments until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to an incision in the vein, one should take some of the pus from the abscess and smear it over all the surrounding skin, and then insert a needle beneath where one is holding the pus on their hand, and pierce it through so that there are two threads, and tie off the artery with a double thread at three places; then lance the abscess so that the excess pus comes out, and then lance the pus from the skin and leave what is tied; then place a moistened cloth in wine and oil over it, and treat it with tenting and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the arteries and veins, they come to the nerves when they are wounded, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and all over where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain; and when one presses on it hard, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the skin; and it is mute everywhere, and does not move forward or backward, or down or up, and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron: by chance there might be contraction; and for that which is on the head or forehead, use the spathumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and squeeze it at its root; and if it is large, slit it with a knife, and scrape it, then cut out the bone and close the wound with stitches, and let it heal.
des grosses boces pendans	large bumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At times it occurs in the belly and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to ears, with thin roots and thick branches. There are both small and very large ones. I saw a man who had two on his abdomen that looked more like fungi than anything else, without any difference between them, white in color, with thin roots, and split open, from which moisture flowed.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces; the treatment for the incision is such that you examine whether the disease is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with thin roots; then apply the spatula widely, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Because there are often excessive bloodlettings when cutting, and if the blood flows, then quickly apply the cautery; and if you see the disease is frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-prepared thread and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop tightening the thread until he cuts the joint, and through him without pain; and if the roots are large, then have fear of cutting the abdomen in the same way, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the abdomen which is of pale color and poor sense and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterizing a wound or a fissure in the sinus, and it is on the abdomen and in some of the bowels, as happens in other routs, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is mentioned above, or from wind; and if it is from the rout of the sinus and from the output of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and it opens from various outputs.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more varied; and when one presses it with their hands, it retreats, and then comes back out, and sometimes it is blocked, and increases significantly at the entrance of the bath and with intense effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, and it does not constrain; and if it is from blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and they are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is from wind, then it is soft to the touch, and the actions are that you should look to see if the appearance is from blood in the artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let it heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is in the intestines or bowels, then you must command the patient to tighten his belly and be stretched out straight, then sign around the swollen area; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the place where you have made the incision all around the spasticity; then stretch out half of the abscess above the string, then tie it tightly with a strong thread or strong silk cord, and release the bowels; then open the other half of the abscess stretched over the string, and probe the intestines; if you find it caught in the string, then untie it and pull out the intestines from the abdomen; and if you find the bowels, then take them at the incision and cut off the excess; and if the artery makes a noise, or the vein, then go around gently, then return to your work and take two needles, and thread them with two strong threads, and pierce through where you have made the cross incision; then pull out the abscess in four places with the needles, and if you see any, remove the needles and let the place heal as it can, and cut away the dead flesh by itself; or when it becomes thin and healable, then clean it as it should be, and treat the abscess as we have said; then draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then clean the area as it should be, and stitch the wound.
dou chancre	from sores
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the likenesses of sores, and how one should work with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure by iron; and we speak of sores which are found in the genitals, and great caution is needed in their treatment. The ancient ones say that when sores are in a place where they can be scratched, like sores found on breasts, or thighs, or similar places, then one should completely remove them when they are in their beginning stage. But when they are large and old, one should not touch them, for I have never been able to heal any such sores, nor has anyone healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the sore is in a place which can be removed, as we have said, it is that you purge the patient with black bile; then make him satiated if there is manifest repletion, then open the sore gently 1 inch wide to perform the operation; then cut the flesh of the sore, and the skin and fat from all around it, leaving nothing behind; and let the blood flow out freely, and press the wound with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding from the artery or vein causes a pulse, cauterize it until the pulse stops; then treat the wound further until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed in the division the appearances of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is caused, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment which is carried out with medicine, and that which is cured by iron. Only these two appearances are mentioned; and one must not use iron on them: they are tympany and hydropsy, for they are deadly conditions. So when you treat this appearance of dropsy, called tympany, with medicines, and the cure does not help, then consider whether the patient is feeble or has another illness besides dropsy, such as a swollen stomach and similar things; in that case, do not use iron, for there is doubt involved. But if you see the patient is of robust health and has no other illness than dropsy alone, and is neither too young nor too old, then one must act thus: lift the patient straight up and press their belly towards the lowest part of their feet to force out the water, then take the spathonis spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cut into two parts. A point, and yet not so deeply that it can reach the intestines when inserted, nor can it cause bleeding; then examine if the hydrocephalus is located towards the intestines: in this case, you should make a cut three fingers' width straight below the armpit; and if the hydrocephalus is due to liver disease, the incision should be made on the left side of the armpit; and if it is due to diarrhea, then on the right. It is important that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the excess fluids do not flow towards the weakened area. Then pierce the skin with the instrument, and insert it, releasing your hand as you move between the skin and the syphons, similar to skinning a finger or an egg; then pierce the syphon until the fluid flows out, indicating the location of the water, then draw it out, and insert this instrument from which the water comes:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver-colored wire, made of thin bronze or light brass, and has in the lower part a small hole; and on one side there are three holes, two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes use to cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top of which is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to a boil, it descends immediately into the instrument; empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is proper at that hour, the patient may die due to the escape of his spirit through the weapon, or he may fall unconscious, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of his strength signify, as well as his pulses; then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the cork that stops the aperture on the syphon, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient enduring it, and draw off a small quantity of water; do this every day, and beware of letting go until there is no more water but a little.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the illness, leave it be and apply hot earth or sand, and with much sweating or bathing in the sun, and drinking tea; and treat with medicines that dry up until he is cured, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening on their penis, or the opening is small and not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If necessary, one must pierce it with a very fine instrument according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put into the opening a subtle plug of lead, and tie it and leave it for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, then replace it; and perhaps this is not needed at all, because the urine that comes out will open it on its own.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose passages are narrow, if they are medicated with a plug of wool, as we have said, will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have an opening in their place are blocked; for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach the urethra, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to do it is for the patient to lie on his back, then the head of the penis and the foreskin are cut to the size of a feather, so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which often occurs, and if it does, stanch the flow of blood, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come on the penis, and they have an unattractive appearance; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must grasp them with a small, sharp knife, and cut away and clean all of them, then put on wet cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, discolored and foul-smelling, then you must apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is within the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the ulcer which is inside; and when it is healed, then cure the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if the glans are not secured so that they are not pierced, and blackness and corruption come to the glans and the scrotum; then one must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply the ointment of honey and flour made from pomegranate rind andwalnuts, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is bleeding, apply the lunar cautery as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery has two purposes: for bleeding and for corruption; and if the glans are腐 and retracted, one must insert a straw into the urethra and the patient should urinate through it; and when there is a sore or an abscess at the tip of the glans in those who have not been circumcised, one must then scrape away the skin with a sharp instrument, so that the foreskin is loosened and the glans is completely exposed; if this is painful to do, then one should scrape it with a spatulum made of wood, at the tip of the glans and through the skin; then separate them gently and place a thin damp linen cloth between them in cold water, so that they do not adhere again.
de la circoncision	On circumcision:
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in that it does not heal on its own; nevertheless, when we perform this procedure intentionally, especially on children, we must do the best and least harmful job.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greater part of masters and surgeons who made circumcision around the foreskin, and in many places, and on any new-born; then the hymen would be cut because there are two membranes, and sometimes one is cut above and the other remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now they recover quickly, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleaning which is done to the foreskin is not secure the tip of the member; and in the cleaning of the nail sometimes the iron slips and they ruin the work, and many times are born thus that they do not need cleaning, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done to the foreskin all over the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly above as below.Or li fuit li doler qui tailla l’ungle, si doit il le tailler par fin et non pas par costé, car par fin il ne se peult mander; si doit il estre tailli par costé, et il faut qu’il soit tailli tant qu’il eschieve la chair.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, you cut evenly into it all around; but the thread should be well-tied around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the rod, and then you make him stretch in all the ways you can; then hold him straight between your hands, and support your weight between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and breathe on the wound, and pull it up until the head of the rod is inside; then cleanse it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place marked with a double thread, then tie it under the other end; and hold it with both hands by the second ligature at the pouch and the index finger, and press between the two ligatures, then lift the wound gently and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the pus; and put powder on top of the powder, a cloth glued with an egg cooked in rosewater, confit with good, fresh rosemary oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it again until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the foreskin after cleansing should be as follows: the two foreskins should be thin and pointed, and the foreskin should be as large as the palm of the hand evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of purification is when the pus within the incision escapes; therefore you must extend it with your fingernail, so that the skin forms an abscess; and then cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, hold it with tweezers and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for 3 days, and what is under the foreskin is swollen, let it be until the abscess has subsided and the skin is slightly peeled; then cut it as much as you can, and beware of the part of the foreskin, it will not harm him in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the area of the wound with a soothing powder, as we have described in the treatise on powders; and if it cuts too deeply into the foreskin, and it goes above, it will not harm; therefore, cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine:
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or congealed blood, or an obstruction in the bowel, or charred feces, or similar causes that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see it retained by a stone lodged at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over on his knees; and his feet placed on his back, and he should press his abdomen from above the back, and restrain himself as much as he can; and this forces the neck of the bladder to expel the stone upwards, thus releasing the urine. If it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use a device called a "syringe", which is crafted like a feather, made of thin silver, as long as a bird's feather; the shaft should be half a palm in length, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the emission of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie to the end a little wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and squeeze out the superfluity of the wool and fill it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or lard and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and squeeze the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upward toward the body; then fill the syringe up to the bladder, and feel the patient's bladder being emptied into the void, and if this is not done according to this order, it is because the leader who guides it is wrong; then pull out the thread all the way through the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is accumulated there, and you see it distilling with water and medicine, then do all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and that is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; and the hair-like channels through which the medicine is administered should be such that it blocks the urethra without addition, so that moisture can be extracted when needed, and injected when necessary. And when you see your medicine moving into the bladder, put the end of the catheter into the moisture, and draw it out as it goes in; then push the catheter firmly back in, and the moisture will follow and enter the bladder, causing the patient to feel it. This is the form of the subtle catheter used for cathartics: thus it is done:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is made of silver or brass, and the end is higher up, below which there is one testicle or scrotum; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture you want to use for cathartics, and tie it between the two testicles with a strong double thread, and heat this moisture over fire. Then insert the tip of the catheter into the urethra and press your hand against the bladder gently until all the moisture goes in, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder. If you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make it into a circle, and pierce it all around; then thread the strong wire through these openings, then assemble the circle as one would assemble a wheel, and put inside it oil, moisture and water, and attach it to the instrument. Do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture goes in.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in the division of stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between a stone lodged in the ureter, and all the signs, and in which type of stone one should operate on the cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder occurs more often in children, and it is a sign that the water goes from the bladder, resembling water in its subtlety; and it seems like a hare's ear, and it hurts the patient its penis, and it can hurt him many times, and then he gets worse; and many of these have the hernia; and the healing is much easier for children until they are 4 years old, and it is much more painful in the elderly, and it is in between youth and old age; and the cure is much easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema to draw out all the feces that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	Because it sometimes clogs up when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and raise him up and move him around so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes out from above; then let him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; then probe and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the passage, then hurry now to cut upon the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out with the touch, then moisten your index finger of the left hand with oil, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young; and insert it into his anus, and probe for the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, push it up to the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and push the stone out where you want to cut.Et s’il adouce li col de la vessie a ton doi indice et qu’il le piege en son fondement, et que tu sens que li piere ne chiet pas, si doit il demourer alai ou tu l’as moue, et que li malade se leve et marche adont qu’il soit bien frotz en li col de la vessie; puis refaites la cure.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to lift the testicles with his right hand, and with his left hand pull back the skin underneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatulum tightly, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they feel in the space between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel; and it lies straight upon the stone, and both hands are pressed against the anus, and the incision is made across the navel so that it is wide on top and narrow at the bottom, according to the size of the stone, not too large; for fear that the pressure from the hand against the anus may cause it to escape without effort. And know that there is a kind of stone which has angles and edges: this is difficult to extract; and there is another kind which lies beneath, resembling a gland, and is round, whose extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are angles and edges on this stone, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, then you must use tweezers like a file at the tip to pull out the stone so that it does not slip away; or you insert below an instrument with a curved tip; and if you cannot grip it thus, then enlarge the opening and apply vitriol, and if there is more than one stone, then insert first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it out, and likewise the smaller ones if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sutured, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: he may die, or urine will escape through the wound that cannot be closed; but still you must try to pull it with tweezers, until you have pulled it in pieces; and when you have finished your work, anoint the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it pressed, and place over it a moistened cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then re-bind the disease over his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, wash the site well with oil and water, then treat the wound with thin ointment and thick ointment until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corrosions come in the wound and blood congealings in the bladder, and it is retained by this, so that urine passes with the blood: then press your finger into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and burst it; then wash the wound with water and garlic and salt, and help him in every way you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that whenever you dress his wound, to tie his two thighs together, and assemble remedies over the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and lodged there, and the urine cannot pass; then the treatment of what I have said above, that you should cut many times, serves as an excuse for cutting with this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this shape and let it be pointed at three angles and fixed in a brand:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis under the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the awl gently into the penis until you reach the stone, and turn the awl in your hand inside the stone a little at a time, until you pierce the stone from another side; then the urine will flow, and press your hand on what is left of the stone that is still inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken at once and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread under the stone and another one above it, then stretch the penis over the stone between the two threads, then pull it outward, and untie the string and clean the congealed blood in the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It sometimes happens that stone is lodged in women's bodies, and if it does, the cure is difficult due to three reasons: one is that the woman might be a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who is knowledgeable enough to examine them, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of midwifery; and the fourth way is that a woman's stone is more deeply embedded than a man's, so it requires a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity arises, one should take a experienced midwife, and with difficulty force her to do it, and if you cannot force her, then desire a wise older woman to examine the patient; or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to do what you command from your examination of the stone. And be very careful if the woman is a virgin: then one should press on her perineum and feel for the stone; and if she finds it, force it out from under her perineum, and instruct her to press and squeeze with her left hand over her bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she has a hernia, it is necessary to move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where the groove is located and feel the stone in that part; do not move your finger above or below the stone, and make the incision small at first. Then open the wound as far as you can feel the stone, and know that there are many kinds of stones: some are small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and some have hairs.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know their appearances in order to understand where they come from.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood comes out, put ground vitriol on it and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task so that the stone can come out, and have some instruments which I told you about in the extraction of the stone from men to help you with your work. And if the blood comes out and it is an artery that is cut, put powder on the spot and constrict it with bandages and a tourniquet, and do not stop doing this, and leave the stone and do not pull it at all because perhaps the patient will die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the pulse has returned to normal, return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rami ce aquo us e is nothing other than the gathering of moisture or white pus, which is under the heart of the testicles and contains the egg; and it is called "sy pha c", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one believes that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white pus which we have said; and this doesn't always happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this disease is weakness which comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it is jaundice-colored, or red-less, or black, or watery white, and that happens more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is in the white syphilis that we have said, then the abscesses are healthy, a little long like an egg, and do not appear to the testicles, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the actual testicle, then the abscesses are healthy with part of an egg, and because of this people think it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white syphilis, it feels good. So when you want to know the color of the moisture, try at all the entry points, from which the shape is as mentioned above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, what comes after the intrusion, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be healed according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back on something slightly raised, and many layers of cloth are placed beneath him; then he sits up on his left side, and the assistant sits on the right, and the rod is stretched towards one of the two ribs next to the heart; then take the spatulum and gently scrape the skin between the ribs down to the breastbone, and make a straight incision through the skin of the ribs up to the white part of the rib, and carefully cut it according to your strength; then pierce the rib with a large hole, and draw out all the water, and then put in your fingers, and stretch the rib upwards; and do not touch the heart, but only the rib; gently scrape all around the rib, otherwise the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have finished the work on the rib; then sew together the two edges of the rib with a single stitch, and then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find that the sac is corrupted by another disease, then you should ligate the vessels that are suspended, fearing the loss of blood; then cut off the testicle at its suspension, and extract it, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If water is gathered in two parts together, you know that they are two bladders; then press the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood and put into the wound soft lamb's wool soaked in rose oil; and put another piece of lamb's wool soaked in wine and oil over it, and place it on the two sides and lay folded sheets over them and tie it up around all the length that is according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two sheets and stuff them with lamb's wool according to this shape and they are sewn together at the crotch of the breeches, and one end is pressed under the buttock up to the back, and the other to the area of the groin; and the two other corners on the two sides, and all the binding is done in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this dislocation is treated with cauterization instead of an iron incision, and it is necessary that you press the small sharp cautery tool onto the skin of the sides, and it is heated as we have said so that the white sac containing the water is exposed; then take the cautery tool according to this shape and pierce that sac at the joints, and scorch it with this fine hot cautery tool.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in every way that you can, as long as you stretch everything out; and be careful not to let the fire touch the egg; and know that this work is safest; and move carefully so as not to cause bleeding, and damage to the surgery of the incision; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscesses or bleeding or anything else, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this treatment because of its horribleness, then administer a perforation as I have told you, and it is that when you are quite certain from the signs which we have mentioned, that the watery pus has drained away, then make the patient sit up on an elevated seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part to the depth of a span, and insert the perforation into the wound deep in the body; and let the openings be large so that all the fluid can drain out; then put cotton over the site and bandage it, and leave it for the remaining fluid to drain out, then treat the wound until it is healed; and if the white membrane does not allow the fluid to discharge through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument used to treat fluid in hydrops patients, the shape of which has been described earlier; and widen the wound, and know that the fluid will return and be reabsorbed after six months or so, and when it is reabsorbed as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this disease there are many complications, due to which I believe it is better left untreated. And I will tell you about the procedure and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come in the body, especially in the genitals; and there are many causes for this.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is caused by an excess of bitterness and bitterness, which is spread in the veins, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are grayish, fearful, and stony abscesses, and a flowing color, and sometimes it comes from an artery, or from inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.Quant c’est de nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is affected by a swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and can be effectively treated with a tourniquet on this appearance and on other characters; and you should press the hollows of the testicles, then the egg is above, and the white part below, and release the suspensory ligament from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already cracked with these new characters, then you must therefore break the egg and press it; and if there is air in the white part, or in what is inside the vessels, then you must release all that membrane and press it smoothly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the yolk is at the back end, then you must open it all and remove the yolk as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is finished, then dress the wound with soft lambs' wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapper similar to an onion, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient feels great pain when he moves; and the cure for this disease is just as fearful as the one before, and yet we will tell you about its treatment according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary for you to make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then tie the suspensory of the testicles down with your fingers, tightly around all the vessels near the penis, and squeeze them hard; then cut through the vessels with a broad, sharp knife, so that they are exposed, and then scorch each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein appeared, and tie it directly to the other end; then draw them gently according to the length of the body, following the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as with the others, or insert a bow, so that any vessel that is bleeding is exposed; for this does not cause harm, and if all the vessels are bleeding, one should draw the testicles toward all the vessels; so that the ureter does not lose its function due to the incision of the vessels, drying up and unable to help itself.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rot of the sinus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this dislocation occur through the section that comes from the hernia, or the extension over the abdomen in the region of the intestines, causing them to descend from this rupture to one of the groins; and this rupture is in the groin, or from the extension of it, and these two types of hernia come about for many reasons: from a blow, or from jumping, or from coughing, or from lifting a heavy burden, and from similar things. The sign that it is an inguinal hernia is that it occurs little by little over a long period of time, and does not come on suddenly; and the abscesses are even all the way to the bottom, because the groin presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs of dislocation of the shoulder blade are that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and there are various abscesses under the skin near the surface, which is due to the exit of the intestines and the body being displaced by the shoulder blade.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the nerves are displaced with the intestines, and it is retained inside, causing great pain to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, one should fear, for which it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;
