puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of treatment is that you instruct the patient to pull the intestine back into the wound with his hand if he can; then hold the neck between your hands and lift the buttocks; then have someone else push down on the abdomen, and spread open the skin of the groin all around; then insert the fingers of your left hand into the opening in the groin, in the space between the white hernia sac and the testicle, and between the second hernia sac, and behind the testicle, and between the second hernia sac; and move your right hand inside the groin, and have the white hernia sac rise up towards your left hand, and lift the testicle away from all of the hernia sacs towards the abdomen; then ask your assistant to push up on the abdomen, and release whatever is beneath the scrotum; and feel with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped around the white hernia sac, and if you find anything, pull it back into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made from ten strands of thread, and insert it into the rear part of the hernia sac, which is under the skin of the groin; then grasp the ends of the threads that appear, so that there are four threads; then tie them together one above the other in the shape of a cross, and tie off the hernia sac with two strong ties from both sides, so that none of the vessels that supply it can enter, causing an abscess to form; then place the second tie according to the first long tie, about two finger widths away; and after these two ties, leave open the hernia sac that is under the groin, the size of a thumb; and after all this, grasp in the area under the skin of the groin, so that the blood flows, as we have said before; then apply soft lamb's wool soaked in oil to the wounds, and place on it the tie that we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white syphilis that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the wound drain through it until it hurts no more; and if it is slow to heal, then apply a poultice of hot water, and keep applying what we have said until it heals; then dress the wound with another dressing until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is done like the ramie fiber which is together with the vein, in such a way that you tie the vessels above lightly after the incision below; then press gently on it, and treat the abscess with what we have described, until the vessels drain; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a hernia in the veins, as we have said, and it opens up; and none of the intestines come out through it, and if some do, it is a little bit, and you repair it every hour; and even if it remains too long in this state, then the wound swells or becomes gangrenous, because of the extension of the gangrene which is in the veins, as we have said, for it extends, then becomes soft and swollen and opens up; and it is treated by cautery, as we have already said; and sometimes it is treated with a hot iron in this way: and you should have the patient lie on his back between your hands, then press the hernia gently with a large piece of cloth according to the quantity of three fingers; then extract the gangrene which is under the skin, then take the thread and place it over the visible part of the gangrene; and press it firmly against the abdomen, then tie the two visible ends of the thread, and tie them one and the other; then pull out the end of the thread, and do not cover the gangrene or extend anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of intestinal hernias; then treat it with wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilis is hidden, and has no appearance in the mouth; and the cautery is effective in this place, and is closer to a cure.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles becomes soft in some men because the parts inside become soft and look swollen; and when one wants to cure it, he should make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin on top of the natural membrane; then bring together the two lips with a single stitch, or three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the stitches.
dou chastrement	from chastity
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is forbidden in our law, and because of this, I would prefer not to discuss it in this book. It is only necessary for two reasons: the first is so that physicians can answer questions about it and know how to perform the procedure; the second is because we often have need of castrating certain animals to help us, such as bulls, rams, goats, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, then, that castration is done in two ways: by pulling or by cutting.Si li atrait a la maniere de l’efile; si le fend a la maniere que je dirai.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In this method of traction, we make the animal stand in warm water until its joints are softened and relaxed; then pull with your hand until they are reset and you no longer feel any resistance.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	On castration: you should hold the animal still and press its testicles with your left hand, then tie off the scrotum, and chop at each testicle until they are well chopped up; leave some of the thin membrane that covers the testicles, and some of the fluid within them; this method of castration is better than traction because with traction sometimes something from the testicles might remain, causing the animal to desire sex; then treat the wound so it heals properly.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in men in two ways: one is where between the testicles there appears the shape of a woman, with hair and sometimes the penis also urinates;
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the little finger as well as a rod and two scrotums.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you bandage all the swollen testicles, and treat them as you would other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine seeps through the scrotum skin, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the testicles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Testicles are swollen testicles on the natural part, so large and unsightly that it is unpleasant to look at; some women have them as big as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the testicle with your hand or a knife, and bandage it lightly; do not cut too deeply so that blood does not leak out, then treat one wound with another cure until it is healed; and there is another swelling that arises in the mouth of the mare, and they use it, and sometimes it bursts, and is similar in appearance to a cow's udder, and so they call it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must cope with it, as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratics
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is errant if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural at birth, or accidental due to illness that comes to it; or it is caused by a wound, or a subtle or thick ulcer, and it is made deep in the head, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and they should understand conception and childbirth, and perhaps flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is through the observation of the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stumps are visible nearby, you can pick them with your fingers or with a stick.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle ulcer and it is nearby the lips, you can treat it as follows: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the lips, so that the subtle ulcer is pulled, and cover the stumps; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the wound, and let the woman stay at home every day, so that it may not adhere.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula like a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is made of flesh, it should be pricked and cut; and have medicines to stop bleeding, such as hemlock, dragon's blood, incense, and egg white; then administer a broad-bladed knife so that the wound does not close; and so for a long time, and then apply a tent of dry linen; then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is flesh damage, it should be cut according to this manner, unless it is an ingrown abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in an ingrown abscess that is in the joint, one must not cut.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are veins that open through which blood flows out, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become thorns; and we have already said in the division their appearances, signs, and I will say here those who receive a cure.Quant la veine est ouverte, si covient que tu la cuites de feu, et que tu li metes une ligature sus le col; et se la veine est trovee, si la peines tant qu’il soit sainz; et quant il est sainz, si peut aler a sa voie.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed piles, when they are deeply embedded in the rectum, and do not appear to the touch, are not cured by the application of a hot iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the rectum, which one can feel, can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore you should put the woman in a cold room; then with tweezers, pull out the hemorrhoid and the throb at its roots; then powder it with blood-restraining medicines such as acacia, dragon’s blood, incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cool water; and if there is any bleeding, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark, gall nuts, and similar things; then take barley flour and mix it with honey and garlic, and make a poultice out of it to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is staunched, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, use cupping glasses on the back and nipples without bleeding them; then take linen, wet it in plantain juice or dogwood juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has settled, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called 'albathir' is red and resembles a hard lump, so cover it as I have said before; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the body, such as ulcers and pus-filled sores, herpes, cysts, and hemorrhoids, as well as hot abscesses, and several other ailments which I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I shall describe in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the body, which is not among the abscesses that collect fluid; and if you want to understand the nature of fire, observe whether the abscess is painful at the beginning of its appearance, and if it is accompanied by heat and fever, and if it turns red when you examine it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let the pain subside; then have the patient sit on a chair with two small seats to lean on, and support his back, and bring his feet together away from the affected leg; let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage. Then suck the wound towards the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the mouth of the wound, from which the shape of the wound will become apparent; when you see the instrument administered, push it in first to determine the depth of the wound, so that what goes into the instrument does not penetrate deeper than it should, nor harm the patient; if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the wound with a piece of cloth so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; then the patient should hold the tip of the instrument and operate it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess has burst open and they have opened it with the hand gently, then it should be covered with a poultice of red lead or white lead; and when the bowels are emptied, then you should put into the wound moist tenters, in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and place the tent outside the wound at the bottom of the injury, and place a bandage over the injury and over the small clean lamb's wool moistened in water, or mallows are cooked; then heal after two days of ointment coming to this, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the injury and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and aristolochia are cooked for a long time; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is depressed into the injury, then you should be careful not to cook with iron, but heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary for the midwife to first know the natural form of childbirth, and the signs that it is about to occur when you see the woman pushing downward, and desiring to smell flowers; then hasten the child's emergence; thus you know that this childbirth follows nature, and the afterbirth comes out beneath the head, and the placenta comes with it; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child emerges quickly; for when it descends upon its head, the placenta comes with it, and the mother is cleansed of her excesses by proper purification; and this one who comes in a different way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out feet first, or the body or shoulder, or hands, or it comes from the abdomen or armpit, and is turned around onto its neck, and in various other evil forms; thus it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and cunning in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how one must assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby emerges head first in a natural delivery, and the woman gives birth with great effort due to her weak constitution, then make her sit on a stool or have other women support her; then apply a warm ointment made from fried oil or fenugreek between the midwife's fingers in the form of a small spatula:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the amnion, and scrape his fingernail until the moisture that is within flows out; and press on the belly of the woman so that the child comes down, and if he does not come down, then one must cleanse the bowels of the woman with a poultice of fenugreek and olive oil; then make her vomit and sneeze with a condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then now deliver the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, then you must reset them gently a little at a time; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet upward; then lean the chair against the ground, and support her so that she does not strain while standing; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then he should scrape the hands with the knife which was mentioned before, and extract the child, and reset similarly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, you should push it upwards; then turn it little by little until it is straight; then grab its feet and stretch it out a little bit at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to its hips, instruct it to grab hold, and make it sneeze with some scent; if it wants to jump out, let God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't jump out as we have said, then slowly turn it back to its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take musk, and oil of sixes, and melted gum, and grind them all in a mortar; and apply this ointment to the nature of the woman inside, then have her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is soft below, make her a collar of myrrh and put it on her, and leave her for an hour; then have her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and squeeze her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	the child will emerge onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the midwife puts her hands on it little by little; then she lies on her side, and the child hangs down with its feet below, and lies on the bed; and she bends her hands little by little, and then presses her hands on the belly, and takes away the cushions underneath, until the child is delivered down below; and if the child does not cry out, she takes its feet and moves it about, then moves the belly upwards, then puts in both hands; and rocks the child little by little; and commands the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the emergence of the child who comes out with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must try to bring the hand back: if I cannot bring it back, then let the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, then let her lie on the bed and lift her legs straight up; then administer the mustard poultice that I described; and if she does not give birth, then let her sit on a chair, then try to bring the hand back again; and rock the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the child's exit above its neck, and spread her hands, and turn her face towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the bailiff to dye his hand, then turn it little by little, and move it gently; and when it is even, put on the natural mustard and oil mixture, as we have said, then instruct her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and tell her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way to all the afterbirth, then scrape away the afterbirth with your nail, as long as the fluids are drained; and if the baby can move on its face and neck, scrape it off so that it is not retained, and the baby dies; then put the baby back inside, so that you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to grip a few times: then she will get better slowly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the hernia
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, but it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange things and do not live, unless by name; I know that they are multiplied and separated by the syrup that divides them, which is bound to the jug; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as a toe, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge quickly, then the surgeon should act as we have said, and be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what he does; and thus proceed as it benefits the patient.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the sea, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the glorious sage; and the surgeon should know all this, for by chance a similar thing may occur; so act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you are treating a woman for a dead fetus or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out by itself, and you are forced to use your hands, then you should know if the woman is of sound health and free from any accident or fear of death; then the woman should be supported on her back, with her head tilted down and her legs raised; and the surgeon should apply the cautery in two parts, or she can be tied to the bed so that she does not move while giving birth to the child; then grease the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with musk-scented aloe and fenugreek and flax seed, then grease the surgeon's hands with these oils and musks; then he should gently insert his fingers into the womb, and probe the locations where it is necessary, and take care that the child is positioned to come out head first; then he should insert his finger into her ears or nose or mouth or throat or under her beard or in her armpits or along her sides; and if the delivery is through the feet, he should insert them at the ankle and the inner thighs; and he should apply the cautery to his right hand, and hold a piece of cloth between his left fingers, and gently insert it into any of the locations we have mentioned, until he reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the probe:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then pierce the other knuckle, or the third if you need to, so that the extractions are even; and then they are even as they move from one side to the other, so that they can exit, and the knuckles are bitten to hold them in place, just like this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then grease some of his fingers with oil and rub it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if nothing remains, then put this knuckle or a higher one, and do this until everything comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back due to the tightness, then you must wrap a cloth around it until it comes out; then grab the end at the joint of the finger or at the wrist, and you should do this for the other hand as well, and also for the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and narrow in its passage, or if it has a sharp pain gathered at its head, then you should push the spathulum between your fingers, open the head, and draw out the fluid; or pierce it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the mold comes with the instruments that follow this one. And in the same way, if the child has a large natural head, then pull on the bones with tweezers, and if the head pops out and is forced, it should be split so that the moisture that is at the bottom of the passage can come out; and if it cannot emerge, then cut it into pieces as much as you can. And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you should pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, the pull is light, and the movement towards the mouth of the wound is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or the foot, you should pull it out with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision in the belly or the foot, as far as the moisture that is there; and if the other members are dislocated, and the feces remain, he puts his hand into the wound up to the bottom of the wound; then he puts in a finger or two, and pulls it out; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, one should not work on it, but rather administer moist and greasy things; and he administers poultices, and uses water that is softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is above its side, and you can make it equal, then administer what we have said about the living child; and if one cannot, then pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the placenta.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the patient is experiencing the abscesses that come in the sea; and if there is bloodletting, let it be applied to water restraining, and give him other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly some fetus had been dead, then another was sewn over it, and the other died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her armpit, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to discharge profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attractive plaster, and an bone came out, and after a few days another one did too.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to see the wound and put my hand in it as long as the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived a long time like this, and she occasionally got out of bed; and I didn't include this chapter until after, because when masters find something strange, they know how to apply a remedy.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the dislocation back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, to which one ties books; and at two turns of the two arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the rest, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the fust should be two fingers wide, and its edges should be smooth, and one palm and a half long; and between the two ends there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are tightly fitted together, each half a palm or a little more in length; and these two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the sea to open it when we turn both horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pincers; it has two joints at each end, as you can see, one palm-length, and two fingers wide. When you see the instrument opened to its full extent, have the woman lie on her back, legs hanging over the edge of the bed, then fit the two joints together inside the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs. Then operate your hand on the instrument, as you did with the pincers, according to the amount you see the opening of the vagina, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated, and their designs vary; and when the patient sees them prepared, the effect is more immediate and more powerful on people due to their appearance.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not be discouraged by the instrument until you have prepared it, for their needs are not preventable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, instruct the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze gently with your hand over her mouth and nose. If she sneezes because of this, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, one takes a pot and makes an opening or lid, and puts in herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as camomile, rue, anise, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then one places a tube or spout into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and lets the vapors enter the wound; then one makes the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the secondine suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not go away, one commands the midwife to moisten her left hand in oil of sesamum or in mullein-mousse, and then put it into the birth canal and seek out the second membrane; and when she finds it, she should grab it and extend it little by little straight, so that the wound does not tear during extraction; but one must move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and release itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is narrow, we have spoken of the cure for sneezing and of the fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from anything that we have said, beware lest you err in the treatment; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the wound, that you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse her with an ointment of the four-part prescription; then she will release and recover, and the foul odor will come out; but nonetheless, when she releases, a foul odor comes to the stomach and the head, and the illness is cured.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If necessary, therefore, appropriate fumigations should be used: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one smokes out the woman for the retention of flowers and afterbirth, if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like glass in appearance, and one puts the fine end into the nature, and the wide end above the fire; and the fumigation is over the charcoal, and the stain until it is wasted, and then one starts another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foreskin pierced, but the skin is closed over a fine shaft; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that shaft with her finger, and not to pierce it with a sharp instrument, and to guard against touching the foreskin; then put wet linen in wine and oil, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, then put a splint of wood through the wound, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to walk.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this healing happens suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be covered suddenly: it should be treated, as we have said, with a splint of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula in the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules which come from under the anus are nodular and grow larger than those which originate from within the anus or between its two parts; there may be one fistula or several. When this nodulation is old, it opens up, and pus and white fluid flow out, or sometimes a thin fluid; these fistulas can be smelly. They can be detected by observing whether there is any discharge or flatulence when the patient breaks wind, and occasionally a smell may escape from one of them.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint, and even to the testicles.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so one can tell whether a fistula at the anus is persistent or not. You should push your finger into the anus and insert a thin needle made of bronze or iron into the fistula if it is straight.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	If it is tortuous, insert a thin and flexible rod or a horsehair until you feel the resistance of the rod or hair at your finger; if you do not feel any resistance and there is no discharge or flatulence, as we have said, then you know that it has not pierced through; so you can proceed with the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends to the bladder or the urethra, and the urine leaks out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced to the joint of the thigh, then there will be a vein bleeding to that spot; if there is no kink and the pain is all around, then it will heal quickly with a poultice; in these piercing fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and foolishness of those who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not pierced and is not old, there is hope of recovery by iron, as I have experienced; the patient lies on his back, and the healer lifts his legs up to his thighs, and bends his thighs towards his belly; then he inserts a tent made of copper or lead if there is a kink, until he finds where the vein is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it in his anus, then you must insert your finger, if you feel that the tent has pierced it; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then you know it is pierced; otherwise, do not work on it, for you cannot heal it.Si la tente ne vient mie par li fondement, si covient qu’on l’estrecce de l’autre costé par la coye, et s’il ne se peut guérir, s’il est persans ou non; car adés il n’y a medicine, ne non plus ne valerat que l’on le saigne, car adés la tentée est persans.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can still heal some of them, although this rarely happens; and the aid that one gives, is that one scorches the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before; and one stuffs it all hot into the fistula, until it comes out through the fundament; and one does this two or three times, until one knows that these falsified meats are burned, which resemble a feather of a bird; and then one cures with moist bandages on butter, until these meats come out, then one cures with ointment binding the flesh and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not healed otherwise; and if the tent comes in, and does not pierce to the bottom which is at the fundament, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of meat or of syphac, and you see the fistula following the covering of the flesh; then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and stuff in before the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it comes to the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered, and fall out; then remove those falsified meats that resemble a feather of a bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus runs out, and flows between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery unites two things: namely, the burning of the joined bones, and the stopping of blood and drying out of moisture; then the treatment of swollen tents with butter or ground substance, until the hole drips, and the burnt bone comes out through the drip; then treat the wound with sudden, hardening oil, and these are the dry remedies.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way from the anus, and is separated from the body, put your finger in it or plug it up, and ask for help.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the membrane or bone, or it is about to pierce, then there is no hope but through the administration of one of three things: either cauterize as we have said, or cut to the bottom, or if you can, place a tent and treat as before; do not go too deep, so that you do not cut into the structure holding the foundation, and let the discharge come out willingly in that direction; then treat as we have said; perhaps it will be healed. Or remove that covering and clean after it has been cut away from the foundation, by tent or other pointed instrument; then mend that broken bone which is in the wound, as much as you can; then work to heal the wound and to stop the fistula in the part away from the foundation: thus the illness will be lighter.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes they are fistulas according to this manner: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation from the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And thread .ii. threads through it, and push the tent all the way through the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that hole so that you put your finger on the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and squeeze them, and leave them for a day or two; and sometimes they are squeezed until the threads grip the flesh between them, and separate; then cure the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, then have it burst in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not appropriate to bandage too tightly and then to treat, as we have said, until it has healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatha or thorn that is used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other; because it should not grip what it should not grab, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be inside the anus, like grains of resin, with both small and large ones, and they draw blood, and some have one or more hemorrhoids, and they protrude from the anus and the top of the anus; but those that protrude have less moisture, and yet they can still draw blood or a little yellow water, and they are colored like the body; and to treat them when they are inside the anus, you should instruct the patient to use the bathroom until the anus relaxes and the veins appear; then quickly grab them with tweezers or your fingernail, then squeeze their roots; if the fingernails cannot hold them due to moisture, then take them with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel hair; then pull them out with your fingers, then squeeze them, and powder them with hot powders that are used as cauterization; you can also cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, then treat other hemorrhoids until they heal; if the anus cannot relax, then cleanse what is inside with a strong and harsh enema so that it can relax completely; when the patient defecates, and if the veins protrude from the anus, then the treatment is simple; grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, squeeze them, then treat them as we have said until they heal and fear incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should administer the suture in the following manner: take a twisted thread and put it through a needle; then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and bring both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be loose; tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, remove the needle, and do likewise with all the others, leaving one to draw off the excess blood; then place a damp cloth in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and command the patient to rest; then leave him as long as he needs to until he has healed, and when he has healed, treat it with ointment and other remedies.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the vagina or anus
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels in the intestines, and due to the constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to cut the skin at the tip of a spatula or your nail; then treat it until it scabs over as it should; and if it cannot scab over, restart the scraping more vigorously than before, until it heals thoroughly and is scoured; then treat it until it has healed.
dou fremit	where it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ant is a small creature that creeps beneath the body and moves very quickly. Sometimes it bites, and one feels it as a tremor, like something dead, and it affects the whole body, especially the hands more than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is to take a feather of a goose or a strong vulture, and place that feather on the tremor, until the purple circle around the tremor; then turn your hand all around the feather, so as to press all around the tremor, and push it deeply, and draw out the tremor by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make it with a cane of bronze or iron according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and drawn out on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, so that it can be held in the hand, and press and squeeze it. And if you see, cauterize the shiver, as it is before in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of molten copper or sheet metal; and sometimes they are made small or large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered to children, the weak and sick, should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema, whether it is small or large, depends on the width of the rectum, according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a hole where the belly is tied, as you see, and the anus is inside pierced; and it has two openings on one side and one on the other; and the belly is where one puts the medicines in a bladder or parchment, pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole is a distance of an inch, then tie it around with a strong thread, twisted in an X or spiral around, and assemble the belly as one does to a goat; and when the medicine is inside, then tie it with a strong string, and clysterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the syringe with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister should squeeze his two hands together simultaneously until they are both empty, then remove the syringe, and let the patient lower his legs to the ground; if the medicine wants to come out, he should hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps for a night, it is even more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the syringe for the sickness of a flowing stomach, and the medicine rushes out, he should repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or rectum, or an abscess, then the syringe should be as fine as for a child; and it is the subtle shape of the syringe that causes the skin to be stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will discuss manual and medicinal cures according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place where the wounds are made, and what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of stones, and cutting with sword or knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or foot, or stomach, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one should take care if it is from a blow of stone or similar objects, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then make the patient bleed with the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and the bleeding should be in the opposite direction from the injured part; and let the patient avoid fullness of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put cotton moistened with rose oil only on the wound, if hot abscesses come from it, or put wine with a styptic agent on it; and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound, if all its blood is fresh and it has not been moved by air.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together by sutures, then bring them together by stitches, as I will describe for wounds in the abdomen, in the rib cage.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and gapes open, and holds only by a little bit of skin, then cut it; next, cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse meats, such as testes and cooked wheat, as well as fowl, and similar things.
