Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut away the rot, and gouge it out; then cure it, and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which causes bleeding without stopping, and medicine does not stem the flow, then tie off the artery, and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: put this powder on so that it will not move until the wound has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is as follows: take frankincense one part, dragon's blood two parts, quicklime three parts, and finely ground it, then apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly so that it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then dress it well and leave it untied if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes cautery is done with a hot iron only, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood; but the wound must be moved by the cautery.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has been moved by the fire, and it is in the same place, do not put any of this powder on it; but apply some soothing ointments, or barley flour made from water and honey, until it feels better; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with thin pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of a wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but let the cure take its course, and not put anything constricting on it, for it hurts the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation with the brain, which is the highest member; but use soothing medicines, such as washed chalk in fresh water, and mixed with rosemary oil, and cooked washed in fresh water, and other stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is chapped and full of pus, then pierce it or cut lower down; and if an artery is cut, and there is a flow of blood, then ligature it and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the food passage is blocked, so that food cannot pass, then cut the windpipe above the cartilage of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then ligature it appropriately, and leave it for a few days, then treat with a poultice until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then drill it out; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and leave those that you cannot reach until the wound suppurates and is cleared and the passage is unblocked; and if the wound is fresh, then apply powder over the powder I mentioned earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine if the wound bleeds profusely: you will know that the wound is mortal. But if the wound is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder in at first, nor ligature it for the bleeding that may occur profusely and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three, or four, or more days; thus no spasms, nor tremors of the heart, nor pains of the body will come. And when you see good signs, then you will know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal and continues to suppurate, you will know that there is a fistula; treat it as such.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, in the front or back, treat it as before; if it is large, sew it up; and if small, treat it with powder, and if it has pierced deep into the bone, and broken off pieces, remove the wound, and the foreign bodies if they are loose; but if they are not loose, let the wound fester to ease the extraction; for other wounds in other limbs, the treatment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium and small ruptures of the belly; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines emerge, through which the intestinal passages occur; and sewing it up is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one must return the intestines into it little by little, as they are more likely to swell when they feel cold, so they return in more quickly; therefore a minor wound is better, as one can reset the intestine to its place more easily than with others.And know that there are four types of ruptures of the belly: the two common sutures occur in the sewing up of the belly, and the sutures of other wounds on the body; and the other two sutures are specific to the belly, and I shall explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestines has come out, and a grievous thing is to be remedied, it is by one of two methods: either due to the smallness of the wound as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in tepid water only, or boil in water with squill and cyprus and spice, and wipe the intestines until the swelling is relieved; and sometimes wine that has been restrained and cooled is useful for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestines with water or altus and malva that have been cooked, for by this there is a constriction of the entrance due to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with an instrument used for hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than cutting, which one should not do without great necessity; and the instrument for splitting it is: insert into the curve and displace it, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out, he puts them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, because it is better that way.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large and it is in the lower abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs above his head; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should be made to lie on his side with his head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture in the abdomen is in one of the sides, then one part should be higher than the other; and thus you should arrange as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use whatever you have available, then take a piece of thread between your fingers and tie the wound's edges together; this is the common method of suturing, and it involves taking a needle with a strong thread, leaving a gap at the head of the wound, and piercing both sides of the skin and the underlying tissue below until you reach the other side, then tying off the thread around the needle so that there is a double thread; then bring the edges of the wound together gently, leaving another gap, and insert another needle; continue doing this according to how many needles you need for the wound's size, making sure the needles are not too thin or too thick, and don't push them too deeply into the flesh or skin so they don't cut or open the wound before it heals; then tie off the threads so that they don't bother the patient when he sleeps, and place tents or pieces of cloth over the needle heads to hold them in place until the wound is healed; this method of suturing with needles is best for small wounds. The second type of suturing is common, and involves taking a needle with a strong thread and tying together the edges of the skin and underlying tissue on both sides at one needle, then bringing the needle back to where you started in the manner that drapes are sewn; space each suture the width of a minor finger; this method works for both men and women, and I once sewed up a man's wound on his abdomen that was cut with a knife; the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines protruded more than two palms out, and the wound was in the middle of his abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestines after they had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was sutured for 15 days, and I healed it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where one could not find any medicine; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and pierce it from the outside into the inside; when it has pierced the skin directly in, then lay hold of the thread on the inside where you inserted the needle, and have it pierce through the other side of the outside layer into the inside. And the understanding of this suturing is that you sew as the furriers do furs, and you leave a turn of the thread on one side, and take it up on the other, until the entire suturing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes correctly, is like that used by some who join two pieces of skin together naturally, and apply one end of a thread to the other, in the following manner: insert a needle at the tip of the nose, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce through from the outside to the inside, at the two tips of the nose; then pierce one and then the other from the outside to the inside, in two other places on the nose that are on the opposite side; this is the correct way to stitch and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some witnesses it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, with a thread in each; and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the sutures are in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound all its blood, so that the burn has moved, then put back the intestine, and the cover; then put on the powder-encasing charcoal, and if the burn has moved, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew the thread, and seal the sutures, and the mirror; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, put on old cotton immediately when it begins to heal bow, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many dispositions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will make community with the principal members, then you should moisten light wool in tempered oil, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the shelves; and if there is pain or porridge in the bowels, and often happens, then enema with warm black wine, and likewise if the porridge comes just to the intestine; and perceive that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine, which is called 'young', cannot heal when it is raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that it has, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the skin tears away from the wound, then put it back as you would with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it has become old and turned green or black, then you should ligate the area that is black so that bleeding does not occur there, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the ligature, and hold the two edges of the wound pendant from the lower part of the wound until it is ready to be extracted when the skin tears, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the road of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, then one can restore it in some people, for I saw a man who was pierced by a lance in the belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became an abscess and fistula, and from it came both defecation and flatulence; I applied a dressing according to what I could, and did not cease to suck until he was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sew up the wound, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain at all but remained in a better condition, eating and drinking. And some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a way: take a thread from a large testicle, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, put it on both lips so that it stretches his mouth; and then tie off the thread, and it will stay as it is so that it cannot come undone. Then put another thread after in the same way until the wound is completely closed, and then cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these sores are in the intestine and do not cause any harm to the patient, then one can sew up the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine in this way: take the end of this intestinal thread which is very dry, then tie it to a fine linen thread which is twisted, put the thread through the needle, pierce the intestine and sew it up; and this method of sewing with threads is certain only according to the hope and expectation. And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the gravelly intestines, there is no health or cure unless with great subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes pus-filled.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green nodule made of a hard white lump, where there is no pain, and it is as swollen as the eye of a bird; and sometimes it clearly pops out, and sometimes it becomes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes quite a lot; and I have already spoken about these in the division of wounds, that any wound that isn't healed and has no pus, this is only due to one of the nine causes: that is, because of the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard matter within it, and on the lips, which does not allow pus to form; or there is too much swelling; or the place is poor, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or because the digestion in the region is slow, and the healing is delayed, and it is swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas can occur in any part of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, from the syphilis, or intestines, or bladder, or any of the sides, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and also those which come to the principal property of the main member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of grief sanation, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it being understood, then take an iron or bronze tent, if the fistula is straight, then probe it; and if the fistula is crooked, then probe with a thin piece of lead, for the lead bends according to the crookedness. And if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot probe it well with tents, then cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses; then press it hard in your hand to the point that you can feel whether there is bone or nerve, and test its depth, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press. And when you know the true location, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, then probe it according to what I have told you, and remove the festered matter and rotten flesh that is inside; then cure it until it is healed. And if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you should probe as deeply as you can, then place moist tents in medical water, and insert them into the head of the fistula to the point that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom. Then apply ointments to promote healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize as we have said. And if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then probe it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve troubles your principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, then treat it with things that warm until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: then expose and probe until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach it; then do nothing but let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone decayed, and you can pull it out with tongs, then extract it with an appropriate instrument for that purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out one by one; and if moisture causes contrary effects, without error or fear, then cut and dry and warm, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, place something over the wound to promote pustulation, and let it fester around the bone, and then the bones will come loose more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, simply treat the corruption until the blackness is gone, then dress the wound; and if a large part of it is rotted away and comes down to the marrow of the bone, it must be cleaned out and packed all the way to the corruption, and then treated until it heals. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years who had pain in his leg from a cause that originated within the body, so much so that the matter came to the leg and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to drain it; but through their folly, the surgeons operated on it until the abscess burst, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared from which pus and moisture from the body issued; and many surgeons treated him for two years, but there was no wise man in the art of medicine among them, so I was called to attend him, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and the matter flowing from the openings into a great wound; and the skin of the young man became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of the openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that some came face to face with others throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and probed one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, which I found to be rotten and pierced, with the corruption extending into the bone; I cleared away what appeared to me to be of the rotten bone, and believed that there was no other corruption besides what I removed; and then began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; so I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, which I cleared away, then removed it, and tried my best to heal the site; but I could not heal it despite probing around the bone for about an inch, and then removing all of its rotten matter; afterward, I healed it with medicines; and it was healed rapidly, and there was no need to restart the treatment except because of the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and due to the fear of death which I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often the blood evacuated, but it was entirely healed, and in place of the bone a hard lump grew, and it was of good disposition and did not cause any harm or discomfort going or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, one should treat it in this way: take a thread and tie it to the head of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to pull it upward; and place another piece of linen underneath the bone, and tie it around the lump that is above the bone, pulling it so that the corrupt flesh is drawn below, and uncovering the flesh above where one sees the need for treatment, so that the thread does not cut into the flesh; and place a hot iron or a wooden plank beneath the bone to press down on the corrupt flesh; and one should continue to treat it in this way until the corruption is visible and can be felt, and then treat it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh all around; then put a fire brand underneath, and then probe from one side of the corruption to the other, and make the incision at the end of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut through the corrupted joint, and probe the bone on the opposite side; and if the corruption is in the area between two joints, there is no need to cut through; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must investigate the corrosion, how it presents itself to you; and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful that the vein or nerve do not cause harm to you; and know that there are many tools for cutting through bones, depending on the structure of the bones, their appearance, their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore one must prepare a tool appropriate to each type of work; and know that your practice will show you the tool you need, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of sickness; so consider the tool you need according to what is required.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head can suffer damage from within or without; and when you have treated this corrosion with remedies, if it does not improve, then cover the affected limb up to the point where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes death or, what is worse, disability due to the defect in the limb. The signs are that the limb becomes black, as though burned by fire; and after the blackness comes the corrosion of the limb, spreading throughout the body. So act quickly to cover it, and if the damage is from the sting of some venomous creature such as a sea scorpion or adder, and the corrosion is on the head, then cover it and do not give it space to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the corrosion does not spread to the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then it is fatal, and there is no remedy but to reduce the amount of poison according to its strength. And thus you should act whenever corrosion occurs in the foot: if it is in the first joint, then cover it after the next joint; and if it is in the foot, then cover the whole foot; and if it climbs up the leg, then cover at the knee-joint; and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy but to bind the patient so that he dies, for the corruption will spread throughout his body. And the way to cover the limb with a bandage is to tie it above and below, and use a spatumile (wide bandage) to stretch one end of the bandage below while another person stretches the other end above, so that the flesh between the bandages is exposed; then cover it with a linen cloth on each side so that the bandage does not touch the healthy skin and cause further damage or abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood flows when you work, then cauterize the area gently, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then tie the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he had a blackness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion started at the big toe of his foot, so that it affected the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot, and it was healed; and a long time after, the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me, and I placed some repulsive things on him after purification of the body, and he could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, for I had hope of driving out the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, returned home, covered his hand, and it healed; and I have heard no other account except that one should do this to others, if they need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it creates a large gathering of pus; then it ruptures and drains, and the pus flows out, leaving the site hollow, like a vessel; the skin above is as thin as a layer of cloth, and does not heal up to the bone or nerve; such an ailment is called a 'sore', but not a 'fistula'; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone in a deep place, then it is called a 'fistula'; and the skin is like a covering over this entire area, and especially when it is thin, like cloth; and it does not heal due to corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the skin is healing and the corruption is not deep, and the flesh is thick, then treat it with a clyster as follows: examine whether the breast is swollen, and the pus that flows from it has a foul odor; then make the Egyptian medicine which is thus prepared: take honey, oil, and litharge in equal parts, and melt them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, dissolve it in water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and squeeze the opening; and leave the medicine there for two hours, then squeeze it out; do this several times until the breast is cleansed and the pustule drained; and if the Egyptian medicine or the ashes of vinegar are not available, then use a clyster of water with honey in which you have mixed a little litharge; or you may clysterize with honey and wine to which you have added some mallow to soften and cleanse the wound, while the wine causes it to drain; and when you have done this, and you are sure that the breast is cleansed, then clysterize with something that will cause flesh to grow in it; take a diaphoretic poultice made with rose oil and wine; or clysterize with other medicines and ointments whose properties I have described in the section on ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small so that the cane of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it with a sharp instrument and apply a tent of the Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened enough for the clyster to enter; and if the wound is very large, then cut and leave only the space where the clyster can enter, and if the opening through which the pus flows is above, then cover it below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are in perfect health, do not allow them to be constipated; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange things so that the bowels move to the lowest place they can reach. For when the bowels are constipated, do not allow them to be constipated, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange things: let the bowels move gently downward, and leave nothing of the bowels behind; take consolative medicines to put over the wound, and have linen cloth covering all the wound; then plug up the opening of the breast more widely than before, then apply an ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the opening of the wound to ease the bowels, but do not remove the large cloth for several days; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the bowels, and learn what comes from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises over the opening of the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and the health is approaching; and then untie it in the morning, or at noon, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows strongly after many days, you can be sure that the breast will not dry up.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons run long after a time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if there are long-lasting wounds in the flesh from which pus oozes slowly, and others that produce the opposite effect; and if a breast swells for a long time without being able to release its contents, you can be sure that it will not heal; and if a breast is swollen and hard, it is due to an impression on the bone or in the limbs, or in the tissues. This is also true of fistula wounds, as we have already discussed.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the nail abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other places; and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then a hard abscess forms, and it runs and oozes pus as far as the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way to the bone; and corrosion extends to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the affected digit becomes swollen and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment is not effective, then you should cut away all the excess tissue that has accumulated beneath the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is very effective if the bone and nail are healthy; but if the nail grows over the wound, and starts to grow into the tissue, and the nail bed becomes inflamed, then you should place a thread beneath the nail to lift it up, and cut away the infected tissue gently and carefully; then apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all the infection; afterwards treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and draw it out, for as long as the bone remains corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone is corrupted, then cut it in half at the joint as has been said before, then cure it until it heals; and if it is broken, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then he must be treated first; then cut the nail of the finger with an incision across the top, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel great pain; and if this happens, then place something on it to soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deaf person's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two toenails that sometimes grow on the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes they have bones in them, and sometimes they have nails, and some grow from the root of the joint where the nail grows from one of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born with a hernia in the navel do not die, but those born with a hernia at the joint of the navel sometimes do; the size of one who is fleshy is slight, in such a way: cut it at its root with a wide spatulum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint, if you hold it tight.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born with a hernia in the navel at the back, you should first scrape away the flesh roundly up to the bone, then scrape the bone to an appropriate size for that, then heal it until it is well.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by wound, or by burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you should scrape that seam so that the intestines return according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened sheets in rose oil, so that they do not adhere; or put between two pieces of thin lead, until the seams are souded, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a person with a sore palm comes to you, then treat that wound as it should be treated.
des vils	of the evil one
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large, enveloped vessels filled with melancholy superfluities, which come from various parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him an emetic, and then the basil drink.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	There are two ways of treating them: one is to cut them, and draw out the black blood; the other way is that you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this way: first, heat the leg with very hot water until the large vessels are dilated, then stretch the leg from the thigh to the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places, with a broad incision, then open and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure; then ligate it, and order that he eat meat mixed with black gall; and repeat the incision and phlebotomy when the veins are refilled, and the patient is worse off.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the ulcer is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then press on the vein from the top of the knee down to the ankle, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the base of the ulcer, and scrape off the ulcer from all sides until it bleeds; and when one sees that it is red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then push the thread under, so that it comes out of the skin, and then pull it gently, as you did before; then make another cut, or more if necessary, then pull and cut at the toe, then draw and lift it up to the second cut; then extract it from cut to cut, until it is all out, then cut it off; and if you cannot pull and lift it, then put a strong double thread through a needle, tie it and pull it out, and push it under the thread, and turn your hand from side to side so that it comes out; be careful not to cut it, because if it is cut, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and harm will come to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put a piece of wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the bone is bent and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one splits the bone must be curved and not cut into the vein; it should be a thick curve as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is angular in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pustules that come under the skin, just as snakes and worms come inside the body, angling between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the wound begins to come out, as well as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound opens, you must wrap a piece of cloth around it from one and a half to two and a half inches, and tie it, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time that something comes out of it, wrap the cloth tighter; and if it is too long, cut off a portion and wrap the remainder, and do not cover the root while it is still coming out; because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and swelling in that spot; therefore this wound should be treated little by little until it is completely healed, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this wound is as long as five or ten inches, and a man came to me whose wound issued for ten inches, and when you cover it, it causes a pus-filled lump, and you must treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein leaks, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and much pus comes out, and from which it bleeds; therefore, treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects oxen. It is caused by a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks through the skin, causing bleeding; and it can be harmful, for when it reaches the eye, it can enter and destroy it. This often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and lanced, you cannot prevent bleeding except when it is incised: therefore, you must tie the area above and below tightly with a strong ligature, then cut and draw it out; and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you do not extract it, cauterize it with fire until it dies. The greatest danger it poses is that it can enter the eye, as we have said; therefore, when you see it approaching the head near the eye, firmly constrict the eyelid, then cut and draw it out. You must also use cleansing medications for the body to dissolve malicious humors, and use cooling foods to counteract the heat of putrid humors.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the inside of her elbow; and soon after, I saw it rise up onto her shoulder like a worm, quickly and brightly like silver when it moves from one place to another. The pain left that spot and went into her shoulder, and then a little later ran through her whole body until it came to her other arm. Then she said that she felt it moving around her body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this illness behave in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it as I did in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and their veins are exposed, and this forced the windiness to appear.
