And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare a strong minister, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with a strap tied above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then binds him with a tight strap above the thigh; and another holds his head with a strap; and they all stretch upward and downward at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This stretching method is common for four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must apply pressure to his back. When the dislocation is in the buttocks, you must support the patient on his healthy side, then place a strap above the root of the thigh, and the part beneath the anus; then tighten the strap upward toward the anus and the scrotum. Then have another minister grab his arms and squeeze the fleshy part of the thigh of the affected leg and stretch it outward forcefully: it will return to its place immediately. This type of dislocation is easier to treat than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot move it in this way which we have said, then tie the patient's two feet together with a strong leather strap over their two heels, and over their two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two inches more than the other; then let him be hung from the end of a pole, and let his arms hang down two arms' lengths; then command a minister to grip the head of the thigh, and have another minister hanging with the patient who grips the thigh strongly, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is restored, let the patient lie down as we have said for those with hernia, and tighten the strap on the affected leg properly, and also on the foot; then put two fires, one at the head and one at the feet, then place the fire between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and have damp cloths laid on, so that he does not burn himself, then extend each minister towards him, and let the minister put his hand on the dislocation evenly.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	Otherwise, place him on a table and press it as we have said in the case of dislocation, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, one should extend the affected leg gently, and according to what I have said; and the assistant puts his weight on the painful joint, then presses with the other hand, and pushes it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the hip, he must not extend his leg downward or raise himself up from the table, but he should lie as though his hip were dislocated on the side, as we have said regarding lying on both hips; and he should lie on his face with the bandage extended as we have said before, and someone should press upon the joint on the table; and when the patient extends his legs, they should be even and parallel; then bring the thighs together, and apply the plaster, and tighten it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen the bandage, and apply the plaster again. If you see that they are even, then tighten it as before, and let him rest for another three days, then loosen the bandage and have him walk comfortably until his limbs are healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is, inside, outside, and behind; it is not dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not stick to his thigh, then you know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee gently; and another minister extends his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he sticks his leg to his thigh lightly; and put the plaster on, and make the leg air to the thigh, and let them heal together for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not work at all until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not at all, then administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes fully relaxed, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and test in front of the part where it is dislocated: the movements should be light, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely healed, you should make the patient sit up straight, and hold his leg firmly by the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and pull the foot upwards nicely; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it comes back, that is good; if not, then start the operation again, because it will come back; and if it cannot come back like this, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the strap firmly in the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it so that it does not slip; then one minister holds the thigh, and another minister stretches the foot with his hands or with a cord tied to the neck of the foot; then each minister stretches equally, and the strap should be placed tightly between the patient's buttocks to hold him steady when he is stretched; then place the mirror evenly in his hand, and another minister holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at its worst, then place the plaster and gauzes on top, and stretch it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle joint, so that the bandages are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, then stretch it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and the patient should be able to walk within four days; and if he walks before that time, there is no guarantee that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful abscesses arise, then you must soothe them as we have said elsewhere, until they heal.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, one should stretch them gently without force, and this is a minor issue.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in the lower back of the foot, then you should make the patient sit upright on a flat surface or table, and place your foot upon what is visible of the joints, then press firmly upon your foot until it is restored; and when it is even again, and there is nothing protruding, then place under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When injury accompanies dislocation and you wish to restore it, many patients die; so do not be presumptuous in the treatment unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and unless you are compassionate and merciful and cautious, nor bold. At the outset, use warm poultices to soothe the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of recovery; but if you see hope, then immediately return the limb to its proper place, allowing the hot poultice to do its work; and when the limb is back in place, administer warm poultices to soothe the abscess and treat the wound as it should be treated with drying ointments. If there is a fracture and broken bones, set the bones and do as we have said for simple fractures; and beware of rushing into treatment out of fear, as I have said, for this can lead to harm according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	So be it.
